   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Black Friday (shopping)</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div>

      <p><b>Black Friday</b> is a colloquial term for the Friday following&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving Day in the United States</a>. Many stores offer highly promoted sales on Black Friday and open very early (sometimes as early as midnight<sup id="cite_ref-midnight_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-midnight-2">[2]</a></sup>), or some time on <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving" title="Thanksgiving">Thanksgiving Day</a>. </p>
      <p>Black Friday has routinely been the busiest shopping day of the year in the United States since at least 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-holiday.icsc.org_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holiday.icsc.org-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-International_Council_of_Shopping_Centers_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International_Council_of_Shopping_Centers-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Albert_R._Karr_1982_p._30_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Albert_R._Karr_1982_p._30-5">[5]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
       <input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_of_the_term_Black_Friday">Origin of the term <i>Black Friday</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin of the term Black Friday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The earliest evidence of the phrase <i>Black Friday</i> originated in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, dating back to at least 1961, where it was used by police to describe the heavy pedestrian and vehicular traffic that would occur on the day after Thanksgiving. This usage dates to at least 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zimmer_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimmer-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-linguistlist239_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linguistlist239-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since early 21st century, there have been attempts by US-based retailers to introduce a retail "Black Friday" to other countries around the world. Retailers outside the US have attempted to promote the day to remain competitive with US-based <a href="/wiki/Online_shopping" title="Online shopping">online retailers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> For centuries, the adjective "black" has been applied to days upon which calamities occurred. Many events have been described as "Black Friday", although the most significant such event in American history was the <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_(1869)" title="Black Friday (1869)">Panic of 1869</a>, which occurred when financiers <a href="/wiki/Jay_Gould" title="Jay Gould">Jay Gould</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Fisk_(financier)" title="James Fisk (financier)">James Fisk</a> took advantage of their connections with the <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant#Gold_standard_and_the_Gold_Ring" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Grant Administration</a> in an attempt <a href="/wiki/Cornering_the_market" title="Cornering the market">to corner</a> the gold market. When President Grant learned of this manipulation, he ordered the Treasury to release a large supply of gold, which halted the run and caused prices to drop by eighteen percent. Fortunes were made and lost in a single day, and the president's own brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Corbin" title="Abel Corbin">Abel Corbin</a>, was ruined. </p>
      <p>The earliest known use of "Black Friday" to refer to the day after Thanksgiving occurred in the journal, <i><a href="/wiki/Engineering_Magazine" title="Engineering Magazine">Factory Management and Maintenance</a></i>, for November 1951, and again in 1952. Here it referred to the practice of workers calling in sick on the day after Thanksgiving, in order to have a four-day weekend. However, this use does not appear to have caught on. Around the same time, the terms "Black Friday" and "Black Saturday" came to be used by the police in Philadelphia and <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester</a> to describe the crowds and traffic congestion accompanying the start of the Christmas shopping season. In 1961, the city and merchants of Philadelphia attempted to improve conditions, and a public relations expert recommended re-branding the days "Big Friday" and "Big Saturday"; but these terms were quickly forgotten.<sup id="cite_ref-Zimmer_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimmer-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-linguistlist239_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-linguistlist239-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-snopes_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopes-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Use of the phrase spread slowly, first appearing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> on November 29, 1975, in which it still refers specifically to "the busiest shopping and traffic day of the year" in Philadelphia. Although it soon became more widespread, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer">The Philadelphia Inquirer</a></i> reported in 1985 that retailers in Cincinnati and Los Angeles were still unaware of the term.<sup id="cite_ref-listserv.linguistlist.org_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-listserv.linguistlist.org-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As the phrase gained national attention in the early 1980s, merchants objecting to the use of a derisive term to refer to one of the most important shopping days of the year suggested an alternative derivation: that retailers traditionally operated at a financial loss for most of the year (January through November) and made their profit during the holiday season, beginning on the day after Thanksgiving.<sup id="cite_ref-Zimmer_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimmer-7">[7]</a></sup> When this was recorded in the financial records, once-common accounting practices would use red ink to show negative amounts and <a href="/wiki/Black#Idioms_and_expressions" title="Black">black ink</a> to show positive amounts. Black Friday, under this theory, is the beginning of the period when retailers would no longer be "in the red", instead taking in the year's profits.<sup id="cite_ref-Zimmer_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimmer-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-listserv.linguistlist.org_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-listserv.linguistlist.org-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The earliest known published reference to this explanation occurs in <i>The Philadelphia Inquirer</i> for November 28, 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In more recent decades global retailers have adopted the term and date to market their own holiday sales.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The day after Thanksgiving has been regarded as the beginning of the United States <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_Christmas" title="Economics of Christmas">Christmas shopping season</a> since 1952. The practice may be linked with the idea of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Claus_parades" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Claus parades">Santa Claus parades</a>. Parades celebrating Thanksgiving often include an appearance by Santa at the end of the parade, with the idea that "Santa has arrived" or "Santa is just around the corner" because Christmas is always the next major holiday following Thanksgiving. </p>
      <p>In the late 19th and early 20th centuries, many Santa or Thanksgiving Day parades were sponsored by department stores. These included the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Santa_Claus_Parade" title="Toronto Santa Claus Parade">Toronto Santa Claus Parade</a>, in Canada, sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Eaton%27s" title="Eaton's">Eaton's</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade">Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade</a> sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a>. Department stores would use the parades to launch a big advertising push. Eventually, it just became an unwritten rule that no store would try doing Christmas advertising before the parade was over. Therefore, the day after Thanksgiving became the day when the shopping season officially started. </p>
      <p>Thanksgiving Day's relationship to Christmas shopping led to controversy in the 1930s. Retail stores would have liked to have a longer shopping season, but no store wanted to break with tradition and be the one to start advertising before Thanksgiving. For this reason, in 1939, President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> issued a presidential proclamation proclaiming Thanksgiving to be the fourth Thursday in November rather than the last Thursday, meaning in some years one week earlier, in order to lengthen the Christmas shopping season.<sup id="cite_ref-congressthanks_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congressthanks-17">[17]</a></sup> Most people adopted the President's change, which was later reinforced by an act of Congress, but many continued to celebrate Thanksgiving Day on the traditional date.<sup id="cite_ref-congressthanks_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congressthanks-17">[17]</a></sup> Some started referring to the new date as <a href="/wiki/Franksgiving" title="Franksgiving">Franksgiving</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> was the first to offer "Black Friday in July" deals on what they called "Prime Day", promising better deals than on Black Friday. Amazon repeated the practice in 2016 and 2017, and other companies began offering similar deals.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Analyst Marshal Cohen of <a href="/wiki/The_NPD_Group" title="The NPD Group">The NPD Group</a> claimed in 2020 that Black Friday is declining in favor of <a href="/wiki/Online_shopping" title="Online shopping">online shopping</a>, and that the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United States">coronavirus pandemic</a> has accelerated this process. The pandemic also resulted in holiday deals being offered over a longer period of time, even as early as October.<sup id="cite_ref-Chang_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chang-19">[19]</a></sup> Fewer people shopped in person on Black Friday 2020, and most business took place online. Market research company Numerator said sellers of clothing, tools and other items considered nonessential during lockdowns were not promoted as heavily because lower production meant less available to sell.<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Analytics" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Analytics">Adobe Analytics</a> reported that online sales reached $9 billion in 2020, 22% more than the previous year. Foot traffic to stores fell 48% in 2020 from last year, according to RetailNext, while Sensormatic Solutions reported a 52% decrease.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id=".22Black_Thursday.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Black_Thursday&quot;">"Black Thursday"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: &quot;Black Thursday&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg/220px-Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg/330px-Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg/440px-Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2057" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gray_Thursday_KF_Walmart.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black Thursday, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>For many years, retailers pushed opening times on Black Friday earlier and earlier, eventually reaching midnight, before opening on the evening of Thanksgiving. In 2009, Kmart opened at 7 pm on Thanksgiving, in order to allow shoppers to avoid Black Friday traffic and return home in time for dinner with their families. Two years later, a number of retailers began opening at 8 pm or 9 pm, on what became derisively known as "Black Thursday". In subsequent years, other stores have followed this trend, opening earlier and earlier on Thanksgiving Day, or remaining open all day, beginning in the early morning hours.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Some retail and media sources have used the terms "Gray Thursday" or "Brown Thursday" instead.<sup id="cite_ref-gray1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gray1-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gray2_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gray2-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brown_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brown-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2014 "Black Thursday" sales were generally a failure, as overall sales for the holiday weekend fell 11% compared to the previous year despite heavy traffic at the stores on Thanksgiving night.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In response, a number of retailers decided to go back to closing on Thanksgiving for 2015, and <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, although it is holding firm opening on the holiday and holding its sale, also pledged to offer the same deals online for those who wished to stay home.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most retailers abandoned efforts to hold doorbuster sales on Thanksgiving in 2020; large crowds have been forbidden under most circumstances since <a href="/wiki/March_(month)" class="mw-redirect" title="March (month)">March</a> due to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_States" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United States">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, major retailers such as Walmart and <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> had already reduced their hours and dropped 24/7 operations in response to the pandemic, and several retailers known for opening on the holiday (particularly <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, which has typically been open regular hours) have <a href="/wiki/Retail_apocalypse" title="Retail apocalypse">rapidly declined</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Analytics" class="mw-redirect" title="Adobe Analytics">Adobe Analytics</a>, online shopping set a record on Thanksgiving Day 2020 with $5.1 billion in total spending, 21.5 percent higher than in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_Friday_around_the_world">Black Friday around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Black Friday around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg/220px-Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg/330px-Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg/440px-Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Black_Friday_2015_Cerdanyola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High discounts at a store during Black Friday
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg/220px-DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg/330px-DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg/440px-DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:DCUSA.Gallery10.TargetBlackFriday.Wikipedia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Interior of a <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a> store on Black Friday
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg/220px-2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg/330px-2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg/440px-2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2008-08-28_Black_Friday_shoppers_at_Wal-Mart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Black Friday shoppers in the morning at <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> store in Durham, North Carolina
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Black Friday is not an official holiday in the United States, but <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> and some other states observe "The Day After Thanksgiving" as a holiday for <a href="/wiki/State_government" title="State government">state government</a> employees. It is sometimes observed in lieu of another federal holiday, such as <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Day" title="Columbus Day">Columbus Day</a>. Many non-retail employees and schools have both Thanksgiving and the following Friday off. Along with the following regular weekend, this makes Black Friday weekend a four-day weekend, which is said to increase the number of potential shoppers. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/SouthPark_(Charlotte_neighborhood)" title="SouthPark (Charlotte neighborhood)">SouthPark</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, is the most trafficked area of the United States on Black Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Black Friday is a shopping day for a combination of reasons. As the first day after the last major holiday before Christmas, it marks the unofficial beginning of the Christmas shopping season. Additionally, many employers give their employees the day off as part of the Thanksgiving holiday weekend. In order to take advantage of this, virtually all retailers in the country, big and small, offer various sales including limited amounts of "doorbuster" items to entice traffic. </p>
      <p>For many years, it was common for retailers to open at 6 a.m, but in the late 2000s many opened at 4 am - 5 am. The early 2010s have seen retailers extend beyond normal hours in order to maintain an edge or to simply keep up with the competition. In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Toys_%27R%27_Us" class="mw-redirect" title="Toys 'R' Us">Toys 'R' Us</a> began their Black Friday sales at 10 pm on Thanksgiving Day and further upped the ante by offering free boxes of <a href="/wiki/Crayola" title="Crayola">Crayola</a> crayons and coloring books for as long as supplies lasted. Other retailers, like <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Express_(store)" class="mw-redirect" title="Express (store)">Express</a>, MK, <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria's Secret">Victoria's Secret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zumiez" title="Zumiez">Zumiez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tillys" title="Tillys">Tillys</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_Outfitters" title="American Eagle Outfitters">American Eagle Outfitters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, Jordan, <a href="/wiki/Puma_(brand)" title="Puma (brand)">Puma</a>, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9ropostale_(clothing)" title="Aéropostale (clothing)">Aéropostale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, began Black Friday sales early Thanksgiving morning and ran them through as late as 11 pm Friday evening. <a href="/wiki/Forever_21" title="Forever 21">Forever 21</a> went in the opposite direction, opening at normal hours on Friday, and running late sales until 2 am Saturday morning.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 2011, when several retailers (including <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kohl%27s" title="Kohl's">Kohl's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bealls_(Florida)" title="Bealls (Florida)">Bealls</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-midnight_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-midnight-2">[2]</a></sup> opened at midnight for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> and several other retailers announced that they would open most of their stores at 8 pm on Thanksgiving Day, prompting calls for a <a href="/wiki/Walkout" title="Walkout">walkout</a> among some workers.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In 2014, stores such as <a href="/wiki/J._C._Penney" class="mw-redirect" title="J. C. Penney">JCPenney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radio_Shack" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Shack">Radio Shack</a> opened at 6 pm on Thanksgiving Day while stores such as <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belk" title="Belk">Belk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> opened at 7 pm on Thanksgiving Day.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Three states—<a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>—prohibit large supermarkets, big box stores, and department stores from opening on Thanksgiving, due to what critics refer to as <a href="/wiki/Blue_laws_in_the_United_States" title="Blue laws in the United States">blue laws</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The Massachusetts ban on forcing employees to work on major holidays is not a religion-driven "blue law" but part of the state's Common Day of Rest Law.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A bill to allow stores to open on Thanksgiving Day was the subject of a public hearing on July 8, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Historically, it was common for Black Friday sales to extend throughout the following weekend. However, this practice has largely disappeared in recent years, perhaps because of an effort by retailers to create a greater sense of urgency. </p>
      <p>The news media usually give heavy play to reports of Black Friday shopping and their implications for the commercial success of the Christmas shopping season, but the relationship between Black Friday sales and retail sales for the full holiday season is quite weak and may even be negative.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, spending volume on Black Friday fell for the first time since the 2008 recession. $50.9 billion was spent during the four-day Black Friday weekend, down 11% from the previous year. However, the U.S. economy was not in a recession. <a href="/wiki/Christmas_creep" title="Christmas creep">Christmas creep</a> has been cited as a factor in the diminishing importance of Black Friday, as many retailers now spread out their promotions over the entire months of November and December rather than concentrate them on a single shopping day or weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On April 23, 2014, "<i>.blackfriday"</i> joined a growing list of <a href="/wiki/ICANN" title="ICANN">ICANN</a> <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domains</a> (such as—traditionally—.com, .net, and .org).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015, Neil Stern of McMillan Doolittle said, "Black Friday is quickly losing its meaning on many fronts," because many stores opened on Thanksgiving, and a lot of sales started even earlier than that. Online shopping also made the day less important.<sup id="cite_ref-Karp_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karp-47">[47]</a></sup> A Gallup poll in 2012 has shown that only 18% of American adults approve of Black Friday, which is significantly lower than the percentage of American adults who approve of the controversial holiday <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Day" title="Columbus Day">Columbus Day</a>, which is at 58%.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day#Shopping" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day §&nbsp;Shopping</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The large population centers on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Mainland" title="Lower Mainland">Lower Mainland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> have always attracted <a href="/wiki/Cross-border_shopping" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross-border shopping">cross-border shopping</a> into the US states, and as Black Friday (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Vendredi Noir</i>) became more popular in the US, Canadians often flocked to the US because of their lower prices and a stronger Canadian dollar. After 2001, many were traveling for the deals across the border. Starting in 2008 and 2009, due to the parity of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">Canadian dollar</a> compared with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">American dollar</a>, several major Canadian retailers ran Black Friday deals of their own to discourage shoppers from leaving Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Star_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Star-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The year 2012 saw the biggest Black Friday to date in Canada, as Canadian retailers embraced it in an attempt to keep shoppers from travelling across the border.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before the advent of Black Friday in Canada, the most comparable holiday was <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day#Shopping" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a> in terms of retailer impact and consumerism. Black Fridays in the US seem to provide deeper or more extreme price cuts than Canadian retailers, even for the same international retailer. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day#Shopping" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day §&nbsp;Shopping</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the United Kingdom, the term "<a href="/wiki/Mad_Friday" class="mw-redirect" title="Mad Friday">Black Friday</a>" originated within the Police and <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a> to refer to the Friday before Christmas. It is the day when emergency services activate contingency plans to cope with the increase in workload due to many people going out drinking on the last Friday before Christmas. Contingencies can include setting up mobile field hospitals near City Centre nightspots.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The term has then been adopted outside those services to refer to the evening and night of the Friday immediately before Christmas, and would now be considered a mainstream term and not simply as jargon of the emergency services. </p>
      <p>Traditionally, Boxing Day had been considered the biggest shopping day of the year in the UK. In the 2010s, several American-owned retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Amazon_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon UK">Amazon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asda" title="Asda">Asda</a>, began to hold U.S.-style Black Friday promotions; in 2014, more British retailers began to adopt the concept, including <a href="/wiki/Argos_(retailer)" title="Argos (retailer)">Argos</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_(department_store)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Lewis (department store)">John Lewis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Very_(online_retailer)" title="Very (online retailer)">Very</a>. That year, police forces were called to shops across Britain to deal with crowd control issues, assaults, threatening customers, and traffic issues.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In response to incidents at branches of Tesco, Greater Manchester Police's deputy chief constable <a href="/wiki/Ian_Hopkins" title="Ian Hopkins">Ian Hopkins</a> said shoppers had behaved in an "appalling" fashion, and criticized shops for not making adequate security arrangements to ensure the safety of customers."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Following these incidents, some retailers began to discontinue or heavily modify their promotions, with Asda stating that it would not hold all of its sales across a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2016, total spending on online retail sites on Black Friday was £1.23 billion, a 2.2% year-over-year increase over 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In 2017, UK retail sales in November grew faster than in December for the first time<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>, Black Friday is known as 'Dydd Gwener y Gwario Gwirion' (Silly Spending Friday).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Mexico, Black Friday was the inspiration for the government and retailing industry to create an annual weekend of discounts and extended credit terms, <a href="/wiki/El_Buen_Fin" title="El Buen Fin">El Buen Fin</a>, meaning "the good weekend" in Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> El Buen Fin has been in existence since 2011 and takes place on November in the weekend prior to the Monday in which the Mexican Revolution holiday is pushed from its original date of November 20, as a result of the measure taken by the government of pushing certain holidays to the Monday of their week in order to avoid the workers and students to make a "larger" weekend (for example, not attending in a Friday after a Thursday holiday, thus making a four-day weekend). On this weekend, major retailers extend their store hours<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and offer special promotions, including extended credit terms and price promotions. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The concept was imported in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> by <a href="/w/index.php?title=EMAG&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EMAG (page does not exist)">eMAG</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://ro.wikipedia.org/wiki/eMAG" class="extiw" title="ro:eMAG">ro</a>]</span> and <a href="/wiki/Flanco" title="Flanco">Flanco</a> in 2011 and became bigger each year. The two reported the biggest Black Friday sales in 2014. eMAG sold products worth some 37 million euros while Flanco's sales totaled 22 million euros. Hundreds of retailers announced their participation in the 2015 campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015, 11 million Romanians say they have heard about Black Friday which is 73% of the 15 million people target segment. 6.7 million plan on buying something on biggest shopping event of the year in Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Romania, Black Friday is one week before the US Black Friday. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Black Friday is little known in India, as its shopping seasons are different. The busiest times for shopping in India (and hence the times with the biggest discounts) tend to be <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a>, followed by regional festivals like <a href="/wiki/Ugadi" title="Ugadi">Ugadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dussehra" class="mw-redirect" title="Dussehra">Dussehra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pongal_(festival)" title="Pongal (festival)">Pongal</a> in South India, <a href="/wiki/Ganeshotsav" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganeshotsav">Ganeshotsav</a> in Maharashtra, <a href="/wiki/Baisakhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Baisakhi">Baisakhi</a> in Punjab and <a href="/wiki/Onam" title="Onam">Onam</a> in Kerala. Over the past decade, <a href="/wiki/Independence_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence day">Independence day</a> sales (on 15 August) have become a large attraction, though most sales in India last for a period of one week.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The growing number of e-commerce websites and large retail shopping centers has contributed to such sales. The big e-commerce retailers in India are trying to emulate the concept of shopping festivals from the United States like Black Friday and Cyber Monday. Flipkart, Snapdeal and Amazon have been offering discounted products on the major festivals in India. December witnesses the <a href="/wiki/Great_Online_Shopping_Festival" title="Great Online Shopping Festival">Great Online Shopping Festival</a> (also called GOSF) for three days where people shop from all the major e-commerce players and large FMCG brands. From 2015, Google has now stopped the GOSF.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The aim was to bring leading e-commerce players on a single platform and boost online shopping in India. Survey<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> during GOSF 2014 suggests that 90% of consumers were satisfied with the exclusive discounts offered in GOSF. According to <a href="/wiki/Google_Trends" title="Google Trends">Google Trends</a>, the interest for Black Friday is rising every year. Comparing the search volume of the term Black Friday in November 2012 and November 2013, the increase is almost 50 percent (22,200 is the search volume in November 2012 and 33,100 is the search volume in November 2013, according to the Google Adwords). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>French businesses are slowly introducing the Black Friday custom into the market.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Discounts of up to 85% were given by retailing giants such as <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> French electronics retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Fnac" title="Fnac">FNAC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auchan" title="Auchan">Auchan</a> advertised deals online, while <a href="/wiki/Darty" class="mw-redirect" title="Darty">Darty</a> also took part in this once-a-year monster sale. Retailers favored the very American term "Black Friday" to "Vendredi noir" in their advertisements.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In 2016, because of the <a href="/wiki/November_2015_Paris_attacks" title="November 2015 Paris attacks">terror attacks in Paris</a> in November the year before, some retailers used the name "Jour XXL" (XXL day) instead of Black Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> An alternative was brought up by some online businesses in 2018, called "French Days",<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> which goal is to replicate Black Friday during spring season (starting around the first day of May). </p>
      <p>On November 20, 2020, the French government finalized an agreement with e-commerce businesses like Amazon and supermarket chains to postpone Black Friday promotions by a week. Discounted shopping promotions were to begin on December 4 instead, after physical stores shuttered during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> were allowed to reopen.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Germany, "Black Friday" retailer advertisements refer to "Black Week" and "Black Shopping" in English with sales lasting an entire week (excluding Sundays when most retail stores are closed). During this sales period, stores keep their normal working hours. Although goods are offered at reduced prices, the prices are not cut significantly more than normal weekly price reductions. Apple was the first company to run a special Black Friday campaign for the German market in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Apple never used the name Black Friday in Germany, but promotes only a "one-day shopping event".<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the first years, mostly internet retailers have used the event as an occasion to attract new customers with discounts, but bricks and mortar stores have already begun to adapt the shopping event. For the first time ever, German customers spent more than €1 billion during the Black Friday weekend in 2016: According to a Centre for Retail Research study, German customers spend around €1.3 billion ($1.54 billion) during the four days from Black Friday to Cyber Monday 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In Germany the term Black Friday has been registered as a <a href="/wiki/Wordmark" title="Wordmark">wordmark</a> since December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2015, Swiss retailer <a href="/wiki/Manor_(department_store)" title="Manor (department store)">Manor</a> was the first to launch a special Black Friday promotion. The year after, most Swiss retailers launched special offers during the Black Friday Week. It is estimated that customers spent around 400 million Swiss Francs on Black Friday 2018. In recent years, Singles Day got more and more important in Switzerland. This shopping day could replace Black Friday as the most important shopping day in Switzerland in 2019<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day#Shopping" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day §&nbsp;Shopping</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Australia the term Black Friday refers not to shopping at all but to the devastating <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_bushfires" title="Black Friday bushfires">Black Friday bushfires</a> which occurred in Victoria 1938–39. Only recently, has it been promoted as a shopping day in Australia by in-store and online retailers. In 2011, Online Shopping USA hosted an event on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>. Twitter users had to use the hashtag #osublackfriday, which allowed them to follow along and tweet their favourite deals and discounts from stores.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> extended its Black Friday deals to Australia. Purchasing online gave customers free shipping and free <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes</a> gift cards with every purchase. The deals were promoted on its website, reading "Official Apple Store—One day Apple shopping event Friday, November 29".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia_Post" title="Australia Post">Australia Post</a>'s ShopMate parcel-forwarding service allows Australian customers to purchase products with "Black Friday" deals from the US and get them shipped to Australia. In addition to this, numerous stores in the country run Black Friday promotions in-store and online throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_countries">Other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Black Friday started picking up in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> around 2013. In 2015, major retailers such as <a href="/wiki/The_Warehouse_Group#The_Warehouse" title="The Warehouse Group">The Warehouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noel_Leeming" class="mw-redirect" title="Noel Leeming">Noel Leeming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Norman" title="Harvey Norman">Harvey Norman</a> offered Black Friday sales,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and by 2018 were joined by <a href="/wiki/Farmers_Trading_Company" title="Farmers Trading Company">Farmers</a>, <a href="/wiki/JB_Hi-Fi" title="JB Hi-Fi">JB Hi-Fi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Briscoe_Group" title="Briscoe Group">Briscoes and Rebel Sport</a>. Paymark, which processes around 75 percent of New Zealand's electronic transactions, recorded $219 million <a href="/wiki/NZD" class="mw-redirect" title="NZD">NZD</a> (US$151 million) of transactions on Black Friday 2017, up over 10 percent from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, Black Friday started as a publicity stunt campaign back in 2010 to increase the sales to the shopping mall Norwegian Outlet. Since the introduction, it has been promoted every year in a larger and growing market all over the country.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Black Friday is known as <i>Viernes Negro</i> in Costa Rica.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, Black Friday was first celebrated in 2012, as a move from the Government to attract local tourism to the country's capital city. During its first year, it was believed to have attracted an inflow of about 35,000 regional tourists according to the government's immigration census. </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_Sale" title="Black Friday Sale">Black Friday Sale</a> is a joint sales initiative by hundreds of online vendors—among them <a href="/wiki/Zalando" title="Zalando">Zalando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Store" title="Disney Store">Disney Store</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galeria_Kaufhof" title="Galeria Kaufhof">Galeria Kaufhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>. Over its first 24-hour run on November 28, 2013, more than 1.2 million people visited the site, making it the single largest online shopping event in German-speaking countries. There has been growing interest for Black Friday in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> as well. </p>
      <p>2014 marked the introduction in Bolivia,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Colombia, Denmark, Italy, Finland, France,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Lebanon, Nigeria, South Africa and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> Black Friday started as White Friday campaign in 2014. </p>
      <p>In 2015, Spain joined with some small retailers. The celebration became more famous year by year, until the big retailers grew. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, Black Friday was seriously introduced in 2015. Some years before, there were already a number of large and small retailers that used Black Friday in their marketing. However, with a total of 35 participating stores, 2015 can be considered the year in which Black Friday started in the Netherlands due to more widespread support of large retailers. The popularity of Black Friday has grown rapidly in the Netherlands. The number of participating stores has increased to over 125 during the Black Friday period of 2017. For the 2018 edition, 166 shops joined the largest black Friday platform in the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2016, Black Friday was introduced in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Black Friday in <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> is seriously marketed by retailers since 2016. Especially online shops have broke sales records during the last edition of Black Friday, which provides a base for further growth of popularity of Black Friday in Belgium. After 2016, Black Friday in Belgium has grown strongly. The participating shops have increased to over 70 during the Black Friday period of 2017. During Black Friday 2018, a total of 119 participating stores were measured in Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Black Friday became widely popular in <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>. There was even a Black week and Black weekend sales in shopping centres. </p>
      <p>Black Friday has been increasingly adopted by stores in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> since 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> although not without its share of inflated prices and other scams, especially in its earlier years, earning the nickname "<i>Black Fraude</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> (Black Fraud) or also "<i>Black Furadei</i>", which comes from the slang word "<i>furada</i>", meaning a "jam" or tough situation, usually involving money. It is also common to hear Brazilian people say that prices on Brazilian Black Friday are "half of the double". However, currently, the term "Black Friday" has become so popular in the country that stores have been under closer scrutiny from consumers and cases of known scams have been reduced greatly<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Scams still occur and the claim of reduced frequency can be disputed. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_Friday_online">Black Friday online</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Black Friday online">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cyber_Black_Friday" title="Cyber Black Friday">Cyber Black Friday</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_traffic_challenges_for_retailers">High traffic challenges for retailers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: High traffic challenges for retailers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Some online stores invest a lot of money in promotional campaigns to generate more sales and drive traffic to their stores. However, they often forget about the high loads their sites are going to experience. According to Retail Gazette, "A number of major retailers' websites went down as they failed to cope with the surge in Black Friday traffic in 2017<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>... This just highlights that some retailers have not taken the necessary steps to prepare for Black Friday. Failing to prepare for peak can cause poor performance, site downtime, and ultimately lost revenue for retailers".<sup id="cite_ref-A_number_of_major_retailers'_websites_went_down_as_they_failed_to_cope_with_the_surge_in_Black_Friday_traffic_in_2017{{nbsp}}..._This_just_highlights_that_some_retailers_have_not_taken_the_necessary_steps_to_prepare_for_Black_Friday._Failing_to_prepare_for_peak_can_cause_poor_performance,_site_downtime,_and_ultimately_lost_revenue_for_retailers_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_number_of_major_retailers'_websites_went_down_as_they_failed_to_cope_with_the_surge_in_Black_Friday_traffic_in_2017{{nbsp}}..._This_just_highlights_that_some_retailers_have_not_taken_the_necessary_steps_to_prepare_for_Black_Friday._Failing_to_prepare_for_peak_can_cause_poor_performance,_site_downtime,_and_ultimately_lost_revenue_for_retailers-99">[99]</a></sup> Such carelessness results in huge reputational damage. Moreover, The 2017 Veeam Availability Report shows that "Unplanned downtime costs organisations around the world an average of R270m annually, up from the R210m of the previous year".<sup id="cite_ref-Unplanned_downtime_costs_organisations_around_the_world_an_average_of_R270m_annually,_up_from_the_R210m_of_the_previous_year_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unplanned_downtime_costs_organisations_around_the_world_an_average_of_R270m_annually,_up_from_the_R210m_of_the_previous_year-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_tip_sites">Advertising tip sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Advertising tip sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Some websites offer information about day-after-Thanksgiving specials up to a month in advance. The text listings of items and prices are usually accompanied by pictures of the actual ad circulars. These are either leaked by insiders or intentionally released by large retailers to give consumers insight and allow them time to plan. </p>
      <p>In recent years, some retailers (including <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/OfficeMax" title="OfficeMax">OfficeMax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_Lots" title="Big Lots">Big Lots</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Staples,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Staples, Inc.">Staples</a>) have claimed that the advertisements they send in advance of Black Friday and the prices included in those advertisements are copyrighted and are <a href="/wiki/Trade_secret" title="Trade secret">trade secrets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some of these retailers have used the <a href="/wiki/Online_Copyright_Infringement_Liability_Limitation_Act" title="Online Copyright Infringement Liability Limitation Act">take-down system</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Millennium_Copyright_Act" title="Digital Millennium Copyright Act">Digital Millennium Copyright Act</a> as a means to remove the offending price listings. This policy may come from the fear that competitors will slash prices, and shoppers may comparison shop. The actual validity of the claim that prices form a protected work of authorship is uncertain as the prices themselves (though not the advertisements) might be considered a fact in which case they would not receive the same level of protection as a copyrighted work.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (November 2013)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The benefit of threatening Internet sites with a DMCA based lawsuit has proved tenuous at best. While some sites have complied with the requests, others have either ignored the threats or simply continued to post the information under the name of a similar-sounding fictional retailer. However, careful timing may mitigate the take-down notice. An <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">Internet service provider</a> in 2003 brought suit against <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kohl%27s" title="Kohl's">Kohl's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target Corporation</a>, arguing that the take-down notice provisions of the DMCA are unconstitutional. The court dismissed the case, ruling that only the third-party posters of the advertisements, and not the ISP itself, would have <a href="/wiki/Standing_(law)" title="Standing (law)">standing</a> to sue the retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Usage of Black Friday Advertising Tip sites and buying direct varies by state in the U.S., influenced in large part by differences in shipping costs and whether a state has a sales tax. However, in recent years, the convenience of online shopping has increased the number of cross-border shoppers seeking bargains from outside of the U.S., especially from Canada. Statistics Canada indicates that online cross-border shopping by Canadians has increased by about 300M a year since 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Statscan_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statscan-104">[104]</a></sup> The complex nature of additional fees such as taxes, duties and brokerage can make calculating the final cost of cross-border Black Friday deals difficult. Cross-border shopping solutions exist to mitigate the problem through estimation of the various cost involved. </p>
      <p>In 2019, Adobe shopping data showed that around 39% of the shopping was done through <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cyber_Monday">Cyber Monday</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cyber Monday">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cyber_Monday" title="Cyber Monday">Cyber Monday</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The term <i>Cyber Monday</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">neologism</a> invented in 2005 by the <a href="/wiki/National_Retail_Federation" title="National Retail Federation">National Retail Federation</a>'s division Shop.org,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> refers to the Monday immediately following Black Friday based on a trend that retailers began to recognize in 2003 and 2004. Retailers noticed that many consumers, who were too busy to shop over the Thanksgiving weekend or did not find what they were looking for, shopped for bargains online that Monday from home or work. In 2010, Hitwise reported: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>Thanksgiving weekend offered a strong start, especially as Black Friday sales continued to grow in popularity. For the 2nd consecutive year, Black Friday was the highest day for retail traffic during the holiday season, followed by Thanksgiving and Cyber Monday. The highest year-over-year increases in visits took place on Cyber Monday and Black Friday with growth of 16% and 13%, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <p>In 2013, Cyber Monday online sales grew by 18% over the previous year, hitting a record $1.73 billion, with an average order value of $128.<sup id="cite_ref-ComScore_Cyber_Monday_2013_Spending_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComScore_Cyber_Monday_2013_Spending-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2014, Cyber Monday was the busiest day of the year with sales exceeding $2 billion in desktop online spending, up 17% from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cyber_Week">Cyber Week</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cyber Week">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As reported in the <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> "Entrepreneurs" column on December 3, 2013: "Cyber Monday, the online counterpart to Black Friday, has been gaining unprecedented popularity—to the point where Cyber Sales are continuing on throughout the week."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Peter Greenberg, Travel Editor for <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a>, further advises: "If you want a real deal on Black Friday, stay away from the mall. Black Friday and Cyber Monday are all part of Cyber Week<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>..."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail_sales_impact">Retail sales impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Retail sales impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Retail_Federation" title="National Retail Federation">National Retail Federation</a> releases figures on the sales for each <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">Thanksgiving</a> weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The Federation's definition of "Black Friday weekend" includes Thursday, Friday, Saturday and projected spending for Sunday. The survey estimates number of shoppers, not number of people. </p>
      <p>The length of the shopping season is not the same across all years: the date for Black Friday varies between November 23 and 29, while Christmas Eve is fixed at December 24. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Friday_(shopping)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/28px-Industry5.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/42px-Industry5.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Industry5.svg/56px-Industry5.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Companies" title="Portal:Companies">Companies portal</a></span></li> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="17" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:United_States" title="Portal:United States">United States portal</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>These are various day-long events similar to Black Friday around the world or any other events on the same day as Black Friday.</p>
